		<ul class="vector-menu-content-list">
			
			<li id="t-whatlinkshere" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/wiki/Special:WhatLinksHere/Enterprise_resource_planning" title="List of all English Wikipedia pages containing links to this page [j]" accesskey="j"><span>What links here</span></a></li><li id="t-recentchangeslinked" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/wiki/Special:RecentChangesLinked/Enterprise_resource_planning" rel="nofollow" title="Recent changes in pages linked from this page [k]" accesskey="k"><span>Related changes</span></a></li><li id="t-upload" class="mw-list-item"><a href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:File_Upload_Wizard" title="Upload files [u]" accesskey="u"><span>Upload file</span></a></li><li id="t-permalink" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;oldid=1335333452" title="Permanent link to this revision of this page"><span>Permanent link</span></a></li><li id="t-info" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=info" title="More information about this page"><span>Page information</span></a></li><li id="t-cite" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special:CiteThisPage&amp;page=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;id=1335333452&amp;wpFormIdentifier=titleform" title="Information on how to cite this page"><span>Cite this page</span></a></li><li id="t-urlshortener" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special:UrlShortener&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FEnterprise_resource_planning"><span>Get shortened URL</span></a></li><li id="t-urlshortener-qrcode" class="mw-list-item"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Special:QrCode&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fen.wikipedia.org%2Fwiki%2FEnterprise_resource_planning"><span>Download QR code</span></a></li>

				<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body" aria-labelledby="firstHeading" data-mw-ve-target-container>
					<div class="vector-body-before-content">
							<div class="mw-indicators">
		</div>

						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Corporate task of optimizing the existing resources in a company</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ERP_modules.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ERP_modules.svg/330px-ERP_modules.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="225" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ERP_modules.svg/500px-ERP_modules.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/ERP_modules.svg/960px-ERP_modules.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="384" /></a><figcaption>Diagram showing some typical ERP modules</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Enterprise resource planning</b> (<b>ERP</b>) is the integrated management of main <a href="/wiki/Business_process" title="Business process">business processes</a>, often in <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing" title="Real-time computing">real time</a> and mediated by <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>. ERP is usually referred to as a category of <a href="/wiki/Business_management_tools" title="Business management tools">business management software</a>—typically a suite of integrated <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">applications</a>—that an organization can use to collect, store, manage and interpret data from many <a href="/wiki/Business_sector" title="Business sector">business</a> activities. <b>ERP systems</b> can be local-based or <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud-based</a>. Cloud-based applications have grown rapidly since the early 2010s due to the increased efficiencies arising from information being readily available from any location with Internet access. However, ERP differs from integrated business management systems by including planning all resources that are required in the future to meet business objectives. This includes plans for getting suitable staff and manufacturing capabilities for future needs.
</p><p>ERP provides an integrated and continuously updated view of core business processes, typically using a shared <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> managed by a <a href="/wiki/Database_management_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Database management system">database management system</a>. ERP systems track business resources—cash, <a href="/wiki/Raw_material" title="Raw material">raw materials</a>, <a href="/wiki/Production_capacity" class="mw-redirect" title="Production capacity">production capacity</a>—and the status of business commitments: orders, <a href="/wiki/Purchase_order" title="Purchase order">purchase orders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Payroll" title="Payroll">payroll</a>. The applications that make up the system share data across various departments (manufacturing, purchasing, sales, <a href="/wiki/Accounting" title="Accounting">accounting</a>, etc.) that provide the data.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> ERP facilitates information flow between all business functions and manages connections to outside <a href="/wiki/Stakeholder_(corporate)" title="Stakeholder (corporate)">stakeholders</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a>, the global ERP market size is estimated at $35 billion in 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Though early ERP systems focused on large enterprises, smaller enterprises increasingly use ERP systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The ERP system integrates varied organizational <a href="/wiki/Systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Systems">systems</a> and facilitates error-free transactions and production, thereby enhancing the organization's efficiency. However, developing an ERP system differs from traditional system development.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
ERP systems run on a variety of <a href="/wiki/Computer_hardware" title="Computer hardware">computer hardware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computer_network" title="Computer network">network</a> configurations, typically using a <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">database</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Information_repository" title="Information repository">information repository</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Origin">Origin</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origin"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Business and technology research and advisory firm <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> is credited for first using the <a href="/wiki/Acronym_and_initialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Acronym and initialism">acronym</a> ERP in the 1990s.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Savin&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Savin-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The term captured a functional extension of two manufacturing-based concepts, <a href="/wiki/Material_requirements_planning" title="Material requirements planning">material requirements planning</a> (MRP) and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_resource_planning" title="Manufacturing resource planning">manufacturing resource planning</a> (MRP II), as well as <a href="/wiki/Computer-integrated_manufacturing" title="Computer-integrated manufacturing">computer-integrated manufacturing</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2025)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Without replacing these terms, ERP came to represent a larger whole that reflected the evolution of application integration beyond manufacturing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Not all ERP packages are developed from a manufacturing core; ERP vendors variously began assembling their packages with finance-and-accounting, <a href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair_and_operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Maintenance, repair and operations">maintenance</a>, and human-resource components. By the mid-1990s ERP systems addressed all core enterprise functions. Governments and non–profit organizations also began to use ERP systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An "ERP system selection methodology" is a formal process for selecting an enterprise resource planning (ERP) system. Existing methodologies include: Kuiper's funnel method, Dobrin's three-dimensional (3D) web-based decision support tool, and the Clarkston Potomac methodology.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Between 2014 and 2018, ERP systems underwent a transitional phase shaped by changes in deployment models, user expectations, and enterprise IT practices. This period marked a gradual shift away from traditional on-premises, monolithic ERP architectures towards more modular, web, and cloud-enabled systems.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Expansion">Expansion</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Expansion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>ERP systems experienced rapid growth in the 1990s. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Year_2000_problem" title="Year 2000 problem">year 2000 problem</a> many companies took the opportunity to replace their old systems with ERP.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WagnerMonk2008&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WagnerMonk2008-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>ERP systems initially focused on automating <a href="/wiki/Back_office" title="Back office">back office</a> functions that did not directly affect <a href="/wiki/Customer" title="Customer">customers</a> and the public. <a href="/wiki/Front_office" title="Front office">Front office</a> functions, such as <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a> (CRM), dealt directly with customers, or <a href="/wiki/Electronic_business" title="Electronic business">e-business</a> systems such as <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> and <a href="/wiki/E-government" title="E-government">e-government</a>—or <a href="/wiki/Supplier_relationship_management" title="Supplier relationship management">supplier relationship management</a> (SRM) became integrated later, when the internet simplified communicating with external parties.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-HaymanERP00&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HaymanERP00-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>"ERP II" was coined in 2000 in an article by Gartner Publications entitled <i>ERP Is Dead—Long Live ERP II</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It describes web–based software that provides real–time access to ERP systems to employees and partners (such as suppliers and customers). The ERP II role expands traditional ERP resource optimization and <a href="/wiki/Transaction_processing" title="Transaction processing">transaction processing</a>. Rather than just manage buying, selling, etc.—ERP II leverages information in the resources under its management to help the enterprise collaborate with other enterprises.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
ERP II is more flexible than the first generation ERP. Rather than confine ERP system capabilities within the organization, it goes beyond the corporate walls to interact with other systems. Enterprise application suite is an alternate name for such systems. ERP II systems are typically used to enable collaborative initiatives such as <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a> (SCM), <a href="/wiki/Customer_relationship_management" title="Customer relationship management">customer relationship management</a> (CRM) and <a href="/wiki/Business_intelligence" title="Business intelligence">business intelligence</a> (BI) among business partner organizations through the use of various <a href="/wiki/Electronic_business" title="Electronic business">electronic business</a> technologies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The large proportion of companies are pursuing a strong managerial targets in ERP system instead of acquire an ERP company.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Developers now make more effort to integrate mobile devices with the ERP system. ERP vendors are extending ERP to these devices, along with other business applications, so that businesses don't have to rely on third-party applications.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As an example, the e-commerce platform <a href="/wiki/Shopify" title="Shopify">Shopify</a> was able to make ERP tools from <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Enterprise_Resource_Planning_Cloud" class="mw-redirect" title="Oracle Enterprise Resource Planning Cloud">Oracle</a> available on its app in October 2021.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Technical stakes of modern ERP concern integration—hardware, applications, networking, supply chains. ERP now covers more functions and roles—including <a href="/wiki/Decision_making" class="mw-redirect" title="Decision making">decision making</a>, stakeholders' relationships, <a href="/wiki/Standardization" title="Standardization">standardization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transparency_(behavior)" title="Transparency (behavior)">transparency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, etc.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Functional_areas">Functional areas</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Functional areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>An ERP system covers the following common functional areas. In many ERP systems, these are called and grouped together as ERP modules:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Financial_accounting" title="Financial accounting">Financial accounting</a>: <a href="/wiki/General_ledger" title="General ledger">general ledger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fixed_asset" title="Fixed asset">fixed assets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accounts_payable" title="Accounts payable">payables</a> including vouchering, matching and payment, <a href="/wiki/Accounts_receivable" title="Accounts receivable">receivables</a> and collections, <a href="/wiki/Cash_management" title="Cash management">cash management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Consolidation_(business)" title="Consolidation (business)">financial consolidation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Management_accounting" title="Management accounting">Management accounting</a>: <a href="/wiki/Budgeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Budgeting">budgeting</a>, costing, <a href="/wiki/Cost_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Cost management">cost management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Activity_based_costing" class="mw-redirect" title="Activity based costing">activity based costing</a>, billing, invoicing (optional)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">Human resources</a>: <a href="/wiki/Recruitment" title="Recruitment">recruiting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Training" title="Training">training</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schedule_(workplace)" title="Schedule (workplace)">rostering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Payroll" title="Payroll">payroll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Employee_benefit" class="mw-redirect" title="Employee benefit">benefits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pension" title="Pension">retirement and pension plans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diversity_(business)" title="Diversity (business)">diversity management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Retirement" title="Retirement">retirement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Employee_exit_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Employee exit management">separation</a></li>
<li>Manufacturing: <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_of_materials" title="Bill of materials">bill of materials</a>, work orders, <a href="/wiki/Scheduling" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheduling">scheduling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capacity_utilization" title="Capacity utilization">capacity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workflow_management_system" title="Workflow management system">workflow management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quality_control" title="Quality control">quality control</a>, manufacturing process, manufacturing projects, manufacturing flow, <a href="/wiki/Product_life_cycle_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Product life cycle management">product life cycle management</a></li>
<li>Order processing: <a href="/wiki/Order_to_cash" title="Order to cash">order to cash</a>, order entry, credit checking, <a href="/wiki/Pricing" title="Pricing">pricing</a>, available to promise, <a href="/wiki/Inventory" title="Inventory">inventory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping">shipping</a>, sales analysis and reporting, sales commissioning</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">Supply chain management</a>: supply chain planning, supplier scheduling, <a href="/wiki/Product_configurator" class="mw-redirect" title="Product configurator">product configurator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Order_to_cash" title="Order to cash">order to cash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purchasing" title="Purchasing">purchasing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inventory" title="Inventory">inventory</a>, claim processing, <a href="/wiki/Warehousing" class="mw-redirect" title="Warehousing">warehousing</a> (receiving, putaway, <a href="/wiki/Order_picking" class="mw-redirect" title="Order picking">picking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Packaging_and_labeling" class="mw-redirect" title="Packaging and labeling">packing</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Project_management" title="Project management">Project management</a>: project planning, resource planning, project costing, <a href="/wiki/Work_breakdown_structure" title="Work breakdown structure">work breakdown structure</a>, <a href="/wiki/Invoice" title="Invoice">billing</a>, time and expense, performance units, activity management</li>
<li>Customer relationship management (CRM): sales and marketing, commissions, service, customer contact, <a href="/wiki/Call_center" class="mw-redirect" title="Call center">call center</a> support&#160;&#8211;&#32;CRM systems are not always considered part of ERP systems but rather <a href="/wiki/Business_support_system" title="Business support system">business support systems</a> (BSS)</li>
<li>Supplier relationship management (SRM): suppliers, orders, payments.</li>
<li>Data services: various "self-service" interfaces for customers, suppliers or employees</li>
<li>Management of school and educational institutes.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Contract_management" title="Contract management">Contract management</a>: creating, monitoring, and managing <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contracts</a>, reducing administrative burdens and minimising <a href="/wiki/Legal_risk" title="Legal risk">legal risks</a>. These modules often feature contract templates, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_signature" title="Electronic signature">electronic signature</a> capabilities, automated alerts for contract milestones, and advanced search functionality.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="GRP_–_ERP_use_in_government"><span id="GRP_.E2.80.93_ERP_use_in_government"></span>GRP – ERP use in government</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: GRP – ERP use in government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Government resource planning (GRP) is the equivalent of an ERP for the <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> and an integrated office automation system for government bodies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The software structure, modularization, core algorithms and main interfaces do not differ from other ERPs, and ERP software suppliers manage to adapt their systems to government agencies.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Both system implementations, in private and public organizations, are adopted to improve productivity and overall business performance in organizations, but comparisons (private vs. public) of implementations shows that the main factors influencing ERP implementation success in the public sector are cultural.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Best_practices">Best practices</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Best practices"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Most ERP systems incorporate <a href="/wiki/Best_practice" title="Best practice">best practices</a>. This means the software reflects the vendor's interpretation of the most effective way to perform each business process. Systems vary in how conveniently the customer can modify these practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Use of best practices eases compliance with requirements such as <a href="/wiki/International_Financial_Reporting_Standards" title="International Financial Reporting Standards">International Financial Reporting Standards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarbanes%E2%80%93Oxley" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarbanes–Oxley">Sarbanes–Oxley</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Basel_II" title="Basel II">Basel II</a>. They can also help comply with the facto industry standards, such as <a href="/wiki/Electronic_funds_transfer" title="Electronic funds transfer">electronic funds transfer</a>. This is because the procedure can be readily codified within the ERP software and replicated with confidence across multiple businesses that share that business requirement.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-IngolfoEstab11&#95;31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IngolfoEstab11-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-MSITSys&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSITSys-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Connectivity_to_plant_floor_information">Connectivity to plant floor information</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Connectivity to plant floor information"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>ERP systems connect to real–time data and transaction data in a variety of ways. These systems are typically configured by <a href="/wiki/Systems_integrator" title="Systems integrator">systems integrators</a>, who bring unique knowledge on process, equipment, and vendor solutions.
</p><p><b>Direct integration</b> – ERP systems have connectivity (communications to plant floor equipment) as part of their product offering. This requires that the vendors offer specific support for the plant floor equipment their customers operate.
</p><p><b>Database integration</b> – ERP systems connect to plant floor data sources through staging tables in a database. Plant floor systems deposit the necessary information into the database. The ERP system reads the information in the table. The benefit of staging is that ERP vendors do not need to master the complexities of equipment integration. Connectivity becomes the responsibility of the systems integrator.
</p><p><b><a href="/wiki/Enterprise_appliance_transaction_module" title="Enterprise appliance transaction module">Enterprise appliance transaction modules</a> (EATM)</b> – These devices communicate directly with plant floor equipment and with the ERP system via methods supported by the ERP system. EATM can employ a staging table, web services, or system–specific program interfaces (<a href="/wiki/Api" class="mw-redirect" title="Api">APIs</a>). An EATM offers the benefit of being an off–the–shelf solution.
</p><p><b>Custom–integration solutions</b> – Many system integrators offer custom solutions. These systems tend to have the highest level of initial integration cost, and can have a higher long term maintenance and reliability costs. Long term costs can be minimized through careful system testing and thorough documentation. Custom–integrated solutions typically run on <a href="/wiki/Workstation" title="Workstation">workstation</a> or server-class computers.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Implementation">Implementation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Implementation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>ERP's scope usually implies significant changes to staff work processes and practices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tech-faq.com&#95;33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech-faq.com-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Generally, three types of services are available to help implement such changes: consulting, customization, and support.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tech-faq.com&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tech-faq.com-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Implementation time depends on business size, number of modules, customization, the scope of process changes, and the readiness of the customer to take ownership for the project. Modular ERP systems can be implemented in stages. The typical project for a large enterprise takes about 14 months and requires around 150 consultants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-carl.sandiego.edu&#95;34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carl.sandiego.edu-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Small projects can require months; multinational and other large implementations can take years.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-SankarImplement06&#95;35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SankarImplement06-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-PelphreyDirecting15&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PelphreyDirecting15-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mass_customization" title="Mass customization">Customization</a> can substantially increase implementation times.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-carl.sandiego.edu&#95;34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carl.sandiego.edu-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Besides that, information processing influences various business functions e.g. some large corporations like <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> use a <a href="/wiki/Just_in_time_(business)" class="mw-redirect" title="Just in time (business)">just in time</a> inventory system. This reduces inventory storage and increases delivery efficiency, and requires up-to-date data. Before 2014, Walmart used a system called Inforem developed by <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> to manage replenishment.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Process_preparation">Process preparation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Process preparation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Implementing ERP typically requires changes in existing business processes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Poor understanding of needed process changes prior to starting implementation is a main reason for project failure.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The difficulties could be related to the system, business process, infrastructure, training, or lack of motivation.
</p><p>It is therefore crucial that organizations thoroughly analyze processes before they deploy an ERP software. Analysis can identify opportunities for process modernization. It also enables an assessment of the alignment of current processes with those provided by the ERP system. Research indicates that risk of business process mismatch is decreased by:
</p>
<ul><li>Linking current processes to the organization's strategy</li>
<li>Analyzing the effectiveness of each process</li>
<li>Understanding existing automated solutions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>ERP implementation is considerably more difficult (and politically charged) in decentralized organizations, because they often have different processes, business rules, data semantics, authorization hierarchies, and decision centers.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This may require migrating some business units before others, delaying implementation to work through the necessary changes for each unit, possibly reducing integration (e.g., linking via <a href="/wiki/Master_data_management" title="Master data management">master data management</a>) or customizing the system to meet specific needs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Thomas&#95;H.&#95;Davenport&#95;1998&#95;43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_H._Davenport_1998-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A potential disadvantage is that adopting "standard" processes can lead to a loss of <a href="/wiki/Competitive_advantage" title="Competitive advantage">competitive advantage</a>. While this has happened, losses in one area are often offset by gains in other areas, increasing overall competitive advantage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Configuration">Configuration</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Configuration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Configuring an ERP system is largely a matter of balancing the way the organization wants the system to work, and the way the system is designed to work out of the box. ERP systems typically include many configurable settings that in effect modify system operations. For example, in the <a href="/wiki/ServiceNow" title="ServiceNow">ServiceNow</a> platform, business rules can be written requiring the signature of a business owner within 2 weeks of a newly completed risk assessment. The tool can be configured to automatically email notifications to the business owner, and transition the risk assessment to various stages in the process depending on the owner's responses or lack thereof.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Two-tier_enterprise_resource_planning">Two-tier enterprise resource planning</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Two-tier enterprise resource planning"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Two-tier ERP software and hardware lets companies run the equivalent of two ERP systems at once: one at the corporate level and one at the division or subsidiary level. For example, a manufacturing company could use an ERP system to manage across the organization using independent global or regional distribution, production or sales centers, and service providers to support the main company's customers. Each independent center (or) subsidiary may have its own business operations cycles, <a href="/wiki/Workflow" title="Workflow">workflows</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Business_process" title="Business process">business processes</a>.
</p><p>Given the realities of globalization, enterprises continuously evaluate how to optimize their regional, divisional, and product or manufacturing strategies to support strategic goals and reduce time-to-market while increasing profitability and delivering value.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ferdows&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferdows-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With two-tier ERP, the regional distribution, production, or sales centers and service providers continue operating under their own business model—separate from the main company, using their own ERP systems. Since these smaller companies' processes and workflows are not tied to main company's processes and workflows, they can respond to local business requirements in multiple locations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-gill&#95;47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gill-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Factors that affect enterprises' adoption of two-tier ERP systems include:
</p>
<ul><li>Manufacturing globalization, the economics of sourcing in emerging economies</li>
<li>Potential for quicker, less costly ERP implementations at subsidiaries, based on selecting software more suited to smaller companies</li>
<li>Extra effort, (often involving the use of <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_application_integration" title="Enterprise application integration">enterprise application integration</a>) is required where data must pass between two ERP systems<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two-tier ERP strategies give enterprises agility in responding to market demands and in aligning IT systems at a corporate level while inevitably resulting in more systems as compared to one ERP system used throughout the organization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Two-tier_enterprise_resource_planning_alternative">Two-tier enterprise resource planning alternative</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Two-tier enterprise resource planning alternative"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>An alternative to a two-tier approach is to use as an ERP system which allows for multiple workflows to be configured for the same function. This allows each operation or division to have its own workflow, say for order entry. This avoids the need to integrate two ERP systems as all divisions and operations are running within the same ERP system.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Customization">Customization</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Customization"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>ERP systems are theoretically based on industry best practices, and their makers intend that organizations deploy them "as is".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> ERP vendors do offer customers configuration options that let organizations incorporate their own business rules, but gaps in features often remain even after configuration is complete.
</p><p>ERP customers have several options to reconcile feature gaps, each with their own pros/cons. Technical solutions include rewriting part of the delivered software, writing a homegrown module to work within the ERP system, or interfacing to an external system. These three options constitute varying degrees of system customization—with the first being the most invasive and costly to maintain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fryling&#95;2010&#95;391–421&#95;53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fryling_2010_391–421-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Alternatively, there are non-technical options such as changing business practices or organizational policies to better match the delivered ERP feature set. Key differences between customization and configuration include:
</p>
<ul><li>Customization is always optional, whereas the software must always be configured before use (e.g., setting up cost/profit center structures, organizational trees, purchase approval rules, etc.).</li>
<li>The software is designed to handle various configurations and behaves predictably in any allowed configuration.</li>
<li>The effect of configuration changes on system behavior and performance is predictable and is the responsibility of the ERP vendor. The effect of customization is less predictable. It is the customer's responsibility, and increases testing requirements.</li>
<li>Configuration changes survive upgrades to new software versions. Some customizations (e.g., code that uses pre–defined "hooks" that are called before/after displaying data screens) survive upgrades, though they require retesting. Other customizations (e.g., those involving changes to fundamental data structures) are overwritten during upgrades and must be re-implemented.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Advantages of customization include:
</p>
<ul><li>Improving user acceptance<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Potential to obtain competitive advantage vis-à-vis companies using only standard features.</li></ul>
<p>Customization's disadvantages include that it may:
</p>
<ul><li>Increase time and resources required to implement and maintain<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Fryling&#95;2010&#95;391–421&#95;53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fryling_2010_391–421-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-BradfordModern15&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BradfordModern15-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Hinder seamless interfacing/integration between suppliers and customers due to the differences between systems<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BradfordModern15&#95;56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BradfordModern15-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Limit the company's ability to upgrade the ERP software in the future<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BradfordModern15&#95;56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BradfordModern15-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Create overreliance on customization, undermining the principles of ERP as a standardizing software platform</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Extensions">Extensions</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Extensions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>ERP systems can be extended with third-party software, often via vendor-supplied interfaces.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BendolyStrat05&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BendolyStrat05-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-LeonERP08&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeonERP08-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Extensions offer features such as:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LeonERP08&#95;58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeonERP08-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Product_data_management" title="Product data management">product data management</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Product_life_cycle_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Product life cycle management">product life cycle management</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Customer_relations_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Customer relations management">customer relations management</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Data_mining" title="Data mining">data mining</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/E-procurement" title="E-procurement">e-procurement</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Accounting_management" class="mw-redirect" title="Accounting management">accounting management</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_migration">Data migration</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Data migration"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Data_migration" title="Data migration">Data migration</a> is the process of moving, copying, and restructuring data from an existing system to an enterprise resource planning (ERP) system. It is a critical component of a successful implementation and requires thorough planning. However, because migration typically occurs near the end of the implementation process, it often receives inadequate attention. The following steps can help structure an effective migration plan:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RamaswamyData07&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RamaswamyData07-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Identify the data to be migrated.</li>
<li>Determine the migration timing.</li>
<li>Generate data migration templates for key data components</li>
<li>Freeze the toolset.</li>
<li>Decide on the migration-related setup of key business accounts.</li>
<li>Define <a href="/wiki/Data_archiving" class="mw-redirect" title="Data archiving">data archiving</a> policies and procedures.</li></ul>
<p>Often, data migration is incomplete because some of the data in the existing system is either incompatible or not needed in the new system. As such, the existing system may need to be kept as an archived database to refer back to once the new ERP system is in place.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RamaswamyData07&#95;59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RamaswamyData07-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Advantages">Advantages</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Advantages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The most fundamental advantage of ERP is that the integration of a myriad of business processes saves time and expense. Management can make decisions faster and with fewer errors. Data becomes visible across the organization. Tasks that benefit from this integration include:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-MeerBest05&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MeerBest05-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Sales forecasting, which allows <a href="/wiki/Inventory_optimization" title="Inventory optimization">inventory optimization</a>.</li>
<li>Chronological history of every transaction through relevant data compilation in every area of operation.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Order_tracking" class="mw-redirect" title="Order tracking">Order tracking</a>, from acceptance through fulfillment</li>
<li>Revenue tracking, from <a href="/wiki/Invoice" title="Invoice">invoice</a> through cash receipt</li>
<li>Matching <a href="/wiki/Purchase_order" title="Purchase order">purchase orders</a> (what was ordered), inventory receipts (what arrived), and <a href="/wiki/Cost" title="Cost">costing</a> (what the vendor invoiced)</li></ul>
<p>ERP systems centralize business data, which:
</p>
<ul><li>Eliminates the need to <a href="/wiki/Synchronization" title="Synchronization">synchronize</a> changes between multiple systems—consolidation of finance, marketing, sales, human resource, and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> applications<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>Brings legitimacy and transparency to each bit of statistical data</li>
<li>Facilitates standard <a href="/wiki/Product_naming_convention" title="Product naming convention">product naming/coding</a></li>
<li>Provides a comprehensive enterprise view (no "islands of information"), making real–time information available to management anywhere, anytime to make proper decisions</li>
<li>Protects sensitive data by consolidating multiple security systems into a single structure<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Benefits">Benefits</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Benefits"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>ERP creates a more agile company that adapts better to change. It also makes a company more flexible and less rigidly structured so organization components operate more cohesively, enhancing the business—internally and externally.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ERP can improve data security in a closed environment. A common control system, such as the kind offered by ERP systems, allows organizations the ability to more easily ensure key company data is not compromised. This changes, however, with a more open environment, requiring further scrutiny of ERP security features and internal company policies regarding security.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-SheSecurity07&#95;63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SheSecurity07-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ERP provides increased opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Collaboration" title="Collaboration">collaboration</a>. Data takes many forms in the modern enterprise, including documents, files, forms, audio and video, and <a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">emails</a>. Often, each data medium has its own mechanism for allowing collaboration. ERP provides a collaborative platform that lets employees spend more time collaborating on content rather than mastering the learning curve of communicating in various formats across distributed systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LeonERP08&#95;58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeonERP08-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>ERP is enhanced decision-making capabilities. By consolidating data from various departments and functions into a single, unified platform, ERP systems provide decision-makers with real-time insights and comprehensive analytics. This enables more informed and data-driven decision-making processes across the organization, leading to improved strategic planning, resource allocation, and overall business performance. Moreover, ERP systems facilitate better forecasting and trend analysis, helping businesses anticipate market changes, identify opportunities, and mitigate risks more effectively.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Disadvantages">Disadvantages</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Disadvantages"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Customization can be problematic. Compared to the best-of-breed approach, ERP can be seen as meeting an organization's lowest common denominator needs, forcing the organization to find workarounds to meet unique demands.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Business_process_re-engineering" title="Business process re-engineering">Re-engineering business processes</a> to fit the ERP system may damage competitiveness or divert focus from other critical activities.</li>
<li>ERP can cost more than less integrated or less comprehensive solutions.</li>
<li>High ERP <a href="/wiki/Switching_cost" class="mw-redirect" title="Switching cost">switching costs</a> can increase the ERP vendor's negotiating power, which can increase support, maintenance, and upgrade expenses.</li>
<li>Overcoming resistance to sharing sensitive information between departments can divert management attention.</li>
<li>Integration of truly independent businesses can create unnecessary dependencies.</li>
<li>Extensive training requirements take resources from daily operations.</li>
<li>Harmonization of ERP systems can be a mammoth task (especially for big companies) and requires a lot of time, planning, and money.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Adoption_rates">Adoption rates</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Adoption rates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Research published in 2011 based on a survey of 225 manufacturers, retailers and distributors found "high" rates of interest and adoption of ERP systems and that very few businesses were "completely untouched" by the concept of an ERP system. 27% of the companies survey had a fully operational system, 12% were at that time rolling out a system and 26% had an existing ERP system which they were extending or upgrading.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Postmodern_ERP">Postmodern ERP</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enterprise_resource_planning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Postmodern ERP"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The term "postmodern ERP" was coined by <a href="/wiki/Gartner" title="Gartner">Gartner</a> in 2013, when it first appeared in the paper series "Predicts 2014".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to Gartner's definition of the postmodern ERP strategy, <a href="/wiki/Legacy_system" title="Legacy system">legacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monolithic_system" title="Monolithic system">monolithic</a> and highly customized ERP suites, in which all parts are heavily reliant on each other, should sooner or later be replaced by a mixture of both cloud-based and on-premises applications, which are more loosely coupled and can be easily exchanged if needed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The basic idea is that there should still be a core ERP solution that would cover most important business functions, while other functions will be covered by specialist software solutions that merely extend the core ERP. This concept is similar to the "best-of-breed" approach<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to software execution, but it shouldn't be confused with it. While in both cases, applications that make up the whole are relatively loosely connected and quite easily interchangeable, in the case of the latter there is no ERP solution whatsoever. Instead, every business function is covered by a separate software solution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>There is, however, no golden rule as to what business functions should be part of the core ERP, and what should be covered by supplementary solutions. According to Gartner, every company must define their own postmodern ERP strategy, based on company's internal and external needs, operations and processes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For example, a company may define that the core ERP solution should cover those business processes that must stay behind the firewall, and therefore, choose to leave their core ERP <a href="/wiki/On-premises_software" title="On-premises software">on-premises</a>. At the same time, another company may adopt a hybrid ERP approach, hosting the core ERP solution in the cloud while moving only a few ERP modules as supplementary solutions to on-premises.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The main benefits that companies will gain from implementing postmodern ERP strategy are speed and flexibility when reacting to unexpected changes in business processes or on the organizational level.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the majority of applications having a relatively loose connection, it is fairly easy to replace or upgrade them whenever necessary. In addition to that, following the examples above, companies can select and combine cloud-based and on-premises solutions that are most suited for their ERP needs. The downside of postmodern ERP is that it will most likely lead to an increased number of software vendors that companies will have to manage, as well as pose additional <a href="/wiki/Application_Integration_Architecture" title="Application Integration Architecture">integration</a> challenges for the central IT.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

</li>
